<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Human Development Index</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">composite statistic of life expectancy, education, and income indices</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

background:none;"> <tbody><tr> <td valign="top"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #E7EEFC; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> 0.350–0.554 (low)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #a0a0a0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Data unavailable</div> </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div>
<p>The <b>Human Development Index</b> (<b>HDI</b>) is a  statistic composite index of <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> indicators, which are used to rank countries into four tiers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_development_(humanity)" title="Human development (humanity)">human development</a>. A country scores a higher HDI when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" title="Life expectancy at birth">lifespan</a> is higher, the <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a> level is higher, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> is higher.  It was developed by Indian Nobel prize winner <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a> and Pakistani economist <a href="/wiki/Mahbub_ul_Haq" title="Mahbub ul Haq">Mahbub ul Haq</a>, with help from Gustav Ranis of Yale University and Lord Meghnad Desai of the London School of Economics, and was further used to measure the country's development by the United Nations Development Program (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNDP" title="UNDP">UNDP</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2010 <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Report" title="Human Development Report">Human Development Report</a> introduced an <b><a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index</a></b> (IHDI). While the simple HDI remains useful, it stated that "the IHDI is the actual level of human development (accounting for <a href="/wiki/Social_inequality" title="Social inequality">inequality</a>)", and "the HDI can be viewed as an index of 'potential' human development (or the maximum IHDI that could be achieved if there were no inequality)". The index does not take into account several factors, such as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_wealth_per_adult" title="List of countries by wealth per adult">net wealth per capita</a> or the relative <a href="/wiki/Quality_(business)" title="Quality (business)">quality of goods</a> in a country. This situation tends to lower the ranking for some of the most advanced countries, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G7" title="G7">G7</a> members and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>The index is based on the human development approach, developed by Ul Haq, often framed in terms of whether people are <b>able to "be" and "do"</b> desirable things in life. Examples include—Being: well fed, sheltered, healthy; Doings: work, education, voting, participating in community life. The freedom of choice is central—someone choosing to be hungry (as during a religious fast) is quite different to someone who is hungry because they cannot afford to buy food.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amartya_Sen_,_c2000_(4379246038).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="414" data-file-width="529" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Amartya_Sen_%2C_c2000_%284379246038%29.jpg/170px-Amartya_Sen_%2C_c2000_%284379246038%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Amartya_Sen_%2C_c2000_%284379246038%29.jpg/255px-Amartya_Sen_%2C_c2000_%284379246038%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Amartya_Sen_%2C_c2000_%284379246038%29.jpg/340px-Amartya_Sen_%2C_c2000_%284379246038%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amartya_Sen_,_c2000_(4379246038).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="404" data-file-width="397" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg/170px-Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg/255px-Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg/340px-Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mahbub_ul_Haq" title="Mahbub ul Haq">Mahbub ul Haq</a></div></div></div>
<p>The origins of the HDI are found in the annual Human Development Reports produced by the Human Development Reports Office of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> (UNDP). These were devised and launched by Pakistani economist <a href="/wiki/Mahbub_ul_Haq" title="Mahbub ul Haq">Mahbub ul Haq</a> in 1990, and had the explicit purpose "to shift the focus of development economics from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_income" title="National income">national income</a> accounting to people-centered policies". To produce the Human Development Reports, Mahbub ul Haq formed a group of development economists including <a href="/wiki/Paul_Streeten" title="Paul Streeten">Paul Streeten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frances_Stewart_(economist)" title="Frances Stewart (economist)">Frances Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Ranis" title="Gustav Ranis">Gustav Ranis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Griffin_(economist)" title="Keith Griffin (economist)">Keith Griffin</a>, <i><u>Farhan C.M</u></i><u>,</u> Sudhir Anand, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meghnad_Desai" title="Meghnad Desai">Meghnad Desai</a>. Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a> utilized Haq's work in his own work on human capabilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">[3]</a></sup> Haq believed that a simple composite measure of human development was needed to convince the public, academics, and politicians that they can and should evaluate development not only by economic advances but also improvements in human <a href="/wiki/Well-being" title="Well-being">well-being</a>.
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:772px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HDI_explained_the_best_way.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="175" data-file-width="985" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2b/HDI_explained_the_best_way.png/770px-HDI_explained_the_best_way.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/2b/HDI_explained_the_best_way.png 1.5x" width="770"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HDI_explained_the_best_way.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The underlying principle behind the Human Development Index.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-5">[5]</a></sup></div></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dimensions_and_calculation">Dimensions and calculation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Dimensions and calculation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="New_method_.282010_Index_onwards.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_method_(2010_Index_onwards)">New method (2010 Index onwards)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: New method (2010 Index onwards)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Published on 4 November 2010 (and updated on 10 June 2011), the 2010 Human Development Index (HDI) combines three dimensions:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>A long and healthy life: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" title="Life expectancy at birth">Life expectancy at birth</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Education_index" title="Education index">Education index</a>: Mean years of schooling and Expected years of schooling</li>
<li>A decent standard of living: <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">GNI</a> per capita (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a> US$)</li></ul>
<p>In its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_Human_Development_Report" title="2010 Human Development Report">2010 Human Development Report</a>, the UNDP began using a new method of calculating the HDI. The following three indices are used:
</p><p>1.<span id="Life_Expectancy_Index"></span> Life Expectancy Index (LEI) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle ={\frac {{\textrm {LE}}-20}{85-20}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>
</mrow>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>20</mn>

</p>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>LEI is 1 when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" title="Life expectancy at birth">Life expectancy at birth</a> is 85 and 0 when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" title="Life expectancy at birth">Life expectancy at birth</a> is 20.</dd></dl></dd></dl>

</p>
<dl><dd>2.1 Mean Years of Schooling Index (MYSI) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle ={\frac {\textrm {MYS}}{15}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>II is 1 when GNI per capita is $75,000 and 0 when GNI per capita is $100.</dd></dl></dd></dl>
<p>Finally, the HDI is the <a href="/wiki/Geometric_mean" title="Geometric mean">geometric mean</a> of the previous three normalized indices:
</p><p><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\textrm {HDI}}={\sqrt[{3}]{{\textrm {LEI}}\cdot {\textrm {EI}}\cdot {\textrm {II}}}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow>

</mrow>
</mrow>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>3</mn>
</mrow>

</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\textrm {HDI}}={\sqrt[{3}]{{\textrm {LEI}}\cdot {\textrm {EI}}\cdot {\textrm {II}}}}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\textrm {HDI}}={\sqrt[{3}]{{\textrm {LEI}}\cdot {\textrm {EI}}\cdot {\textrm {II}}}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/364ecd910bf260a13250cde6a9d25e08d9633fe8" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:21.375ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>
</p><p><small>LE: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" title="Life expectancy at birth">Life expectancy at birth</a><br/>
MYS: Mean years of schooling (i.e. years that a person aged 25 or older has spent in formal education)<br/>
EYS: Expected years of schooling (i.e. total expected years of schooling for children under 18 years of age)<br/>
GNIpc: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GNI_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GNI (PPP) per capita">Gross national income at purchasing power parity per capita</a></small>
</p>
<h3><span id="Old_method_.28before_2010_Index.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_method_(before_2010_Index)">Old method (before 2010 Index)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Old method (before 2010 Index)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The HDI combined three dimensions last used in its 2009 Report:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth, as an index of population health and longevity to HDI</li>
<li>Knowledge and education, as measured by the adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate (with two-thirds weighting) and the combined primary, secondary, and tertiary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_enrollment_ratio" title="Gross enrollment ratio">gross enrollment ratio</a> (with one-third weighting).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">Standard of living</a>, as indicated by the <a href="/wiki/Natural_logarithm" title="Natural logarithm">natural logarithm</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> <a href="/wiki/Per_capita" title="Per capita">per capita</a> at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>.</li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Human_Development_Index_trends.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1152" data-file-width="1179" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Human_Development_Index_trends.svg/280px-Human_Development_Index_trends.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Human_Development_Index_trends.svg/420px-Human_Development_Index_trends.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Human_Development_Index_trends.svg/560px-Human_Development_Index_trends.svg.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Human_Development_Index_trends.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>HDI trends between 1975 and 2004  <table style="width:100%;"> <tbody><tr> <td valign="top"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:black; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> not in the OECD and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #E45600; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #D09B00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a></div> </td> <td valign="top"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00FF00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #003FD9; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C600FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a></div> </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div>
<p>This methodology was used by the UNDP until their 2011 report.
</p><p>The formula defining the HDI is promulgated by the United Nations Development Programme (<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">UNDP</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In general, to transform a raw <a href="/wiki/Variable_(mathematics)" title="Variable (mathematics)">variable</a>, say <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>, into a unit-free <a href="/wiki/Index_(economics)" title="Index (economics)">index</a> between 0 and 1 (which allows different indices to be added together), the following <a href="/wiki/Formula" title="Formula">formula</a> is used:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x{\text{ index}}={\frac {x-a}{b-a}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext> index</mtext>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>a</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow>

<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>a</mi>
</mrow>
</mfrac>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x{\text{ index}}={\frac {x-a}{b-a}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle x{\text{ index}}={\frac {x-a}{b-a}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/649cc3be2e96c9683d44387a699f36a4269c22a5" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:16.737ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span></li></ul>
<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>a</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="a" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ffd2487510aa438433a2579450ab2b3d557e5edc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.23ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>b</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f11423fbb2e967f986e36804a8ae4271734917c3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.998ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> are the <a href="/wiki/Maxima_and_minima" title="Maxima and minima">lowest and highest values</a> the variable <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> can attain, respectively.
</p><p>The Human Development Index (HDI) then represents the uniformly weighted sum with ​<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>3</sub></span> contributed by each of the following factor indices:

<p>Other organizations/companies may include other factors, such as infant mortality, which produces a different HDI.

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_Human_Development_Index">2018 Human Development Index</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2018 Human Development Index">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a></div>
<p>The 2018 Human Development Report by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> was released on 14 September 2018, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-12">[12]</a></sup> Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/> = increase.</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/> = steady.</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/> = decrease.</li>
<li>The number in parentheses represents the number of ranks the country has climbed (up or down) relative to the ranking in the year of 2016.</li></ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI">Inequality-adjusted HDI</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Inequality-adjusted HDI">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2018_Complete_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-2018_Complete-14">[14]</a></sup> is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account".
</p><p><small>The rankings are not relative to the HDI list above due to the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data (p. 30).</small>
</p>

</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_Human_Development_Index">2016 Human Development Index</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2016 Human Development Index">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a></div>
<p>The 2016 Human Development Report by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> was released on 21 March 2017, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2015. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/> = increase.</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/> = steady.</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/> = decrease.</li>
<li>The number in parentheses represents the number of ranks the country has climbed (up or down) relative to the ranking in the 2015 report.</li></ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_2">Inequality-adjusted HDI</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Inequality-adjusted HDI">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016_Complete_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-2016_Complete-16">[16]</a></sup> is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account".
</p><p><small>The rankings are not relative to the HDI list above due to the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data (p. 206).</small>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_Human_Development_Index">2015 Human Development Index</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2015 Human Development Index">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a></div>
<p>The 2015 Human Development Report by the United Nations Development Programme was released on 14 December 2015, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2014. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015_Complete_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Complete-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macau_in_Figures,_2015_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_in_Figures,_2015-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dgbas2011_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-dgbas2011-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/> = increase.</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/> = steady.</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/> = decrease.</li>
<li>The number in brackets represents the number of ranks the country has climbed (up or down) relative to the ranking in the 2014 report.</li></ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_3">Inequality-adjusted HDI</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Inequality-adjusted HDI">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015_Complete_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Complete-17">[17]</a></sup> is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account".
</p><p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/>), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/>), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/>) represent changes in rank. The rankings are not relative to the HDI list above due to the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data (p. 216).</small>
</p>

</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_Human_Development_Index">2014 Human Development Index</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2014 Human Development Index">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The 2014 Human Development Report by the United Nations Development Programme was released on 24 July 2014 and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2013. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries or regions:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_Complete_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-2014_Complete-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macau_in_Figures,_2015_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_in_Figures,_2015-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dgbas2011_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-dgbas2011-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/> = increase.</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/> = steady.</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/> = decrease.</li>
<li>The number in brackets represents the number of ranks the country or region has climbed (up or down) relative to the ranking in the 2013 report.</li></ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_not_included">Countries not included</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Countries not included">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some countries were not included for various reasons, primarily due to the lack of necessary data. The following United Nations Member States were not included in the 2014 report:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_Complete_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-2014_Complete-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_4">Inequality-adjusted HDI</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Inequality-adjusted HDI">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_Complete_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-2014_Complete-23">[23]</a></sup> is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account".
</p><p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/>), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/>), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/>) represent changes in rank. The rankings are not relative to the HDI list above due to the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data (p. 168).</small>
</p>

<p>Countries in the top quartile of HDI ("very high human development" group) with a missing IHDI: <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_top_countries">Past top countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Past top countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The list below displays the top-ranked country from each year of the Human Development Index. <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> has been ranked the highest fourteen times, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> eight times, and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> three times. <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> has been ranked highest twice.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_each_original_HDI">In each original HDI</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: In each original HDI">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The year represents when the report was published. In parentheses is the year for which the index was calculated.

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_coverage">Geographical coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Geographical coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The HDI has extended its geographical coverage: David Hastings, of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Commission_for_Asia_and_the_Pacific" title="United Nations Economic and Social Commission for Asia and the Pacific">United Nations Economic and Social Commission for Asia and the Pacific</a>, published a report geographically extending the HDI to 230+ economies, whereas the UNDP HDI for 2009 enumerates 182 economies and coverage for the 2010 HDI dropped to 169 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="522" data-file-width="850" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg/220px-Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg/330px-Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg/440px-Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>HDI vs. <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Human Development Index has been criticized on a number of grounds, including alleged lack of consideration of technological development or contributions to the human civilization, focusing exclusively on national performance and ranking, lack of attention to development from a global perspective, measurement error of the underlying statistics, and on the UNDP's changes in formula which can lead to severe misclassification in the categorisation of 'low', 'medium', 'high' or 'very high' human development countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolff_et_al._2011_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wolff_et_al._2011-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sources_of_data_error">Sources of data error</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sources of data error">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Economists Hendrik Wolff, Howard Chong and <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Auffhammer" title="Maximilian Auffhammer">Maximilian Auffhammer</a> discuss the HDI from the perspective of data error in the underlying health, education and income statistics used to construct the HDI. They identified three sources of data error which are due to (i) data updating, (ii) formula revisions and (iii) thresholds to classify a country's development status and conclude that 11%, 21% and 34% of all countries can be interpreted as currently misclassified in the development bins due to the three sources of data error, respectively. The authors suggest that the United Nations should discontinue the practice of classifying countries into development bins because: the cut-off values seem arbitrary, can provide incentives for strategic behavior in reporting official statistics, and have the potential to misguide politicians, investors, charity donors and the public who use the HDI at large.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolff_et_al._2011_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wolff_et_al._2011-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, the UNDP reacted to the criticism and updated the thresholds to classify nations as low, medium, and high human development countries. In a comment to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> in early January 2011, the Human Development Report Office responded<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> to a 6 January 2011 article in the magazine<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> which discusses the Wolff <i>et al.</i> paper. The Human Development Report Office states that they undertook a systematic revision of the methods used for the calculation of the HDI, and that the new methodology directly addresses the critique by Wolff <i>et al.</i> in that it generates a system for continuously updating the human-development categories whenever formula or data revisions take place.
</p><p>In 2013, Salvatore Monni and Alessandro Spaventa emphasized that in the debate of GDP versus HDI, it is often forgotten that these are both external indicators that prioritize different benchmarks upon which the quantification of societal welfare can be predicated. The larger question is whether it is possible to shift the focus of policy from a battle between competing paradigms to a mechanism for eliciting information on well-being directly from the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Monni_and_Spaventa,_2013_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Monni_and_Spaventa,_2013-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Mean years of schooling (of adults) (years) is a calculation of the average number of years of education received by people ages 25 and older in their lifetime based on education attainment levels of the population converted into years of schooling based on theoretical duration of each level of education attended. Source: <cite class="citation journal"><a href="/wiki/Robert_Barro" title="Robert Barro">Barro, R. J.</a>; Lee, J.-W. (2010). <a class="external text" href="http://www.nber.org/papers/w15902" rel="nofollow">"A New Data Set of Educational Attainment in the World, 1950–2010"</a>. <i>NBER Working Paper No. 15902</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=NBER+Working+Paper+No.+15902&amp;rft.atitle=A+New+Data+Set+of+Educational+Attainment+in+the+World%2C+1950%E2%80%932010&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.aulast=Barro&amp;rft.aufirst=R.+J.&amp;rft.au=Lee%2C+J.-W.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.nber.org%2Fpapers%2Fw15902&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+Development+Index"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">(ESYI is a calculation of the number of years a child is expected to attend school, or university, including the years spent on repetition. It is the sum of the age-specific enrollment ratios for primary, secondary, post-secondary non-tertiary and tertiary education and is calculated assuming the prevailing patterns of age-specific enrollment rates were to stay the same throughout the child's life. Expected years of schooling is capped at 18 years. (Source: UNESCO Institute for Statistics (2010). Correspondence on education indicators. March. Montreal.)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://hdr.undp.org/en/statistics/faq/question,68,en.html" rel="nofollow">Definition, Calculator, etc. at UNDP site</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071220162154/http://hdr.undp.org/en/statistics/faq/question%2C68%2Cen.html" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 20 December 2007 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>.</span>
</li>

Taiwan's government calculated its HDI to be 0.882, based on 2010 new methodology of UNDP. <cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.dgbas.gov.tw/public/Data/491716362790WG0X9I.pdf" rel="nofollow">"2011中華民國人類發展指數 (HDI)"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> (in Chinese). <td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikimedia Commons has media related to <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Human_Development_Index" title="commons:Category:Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a></b></i>.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul><li><a class="external text" href="http://hdr.undp.org/en/content/human-development-index-hdi" rel="nofollow">Human Development Index</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://hdr.undp.org/en/statistics/" rel="nofollow">Human Development Tools and Rankings</a></li>
<li><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://hdr.undp.org/en/media/hdr_20072008_tech_note_1.pdf" rel="nofollow">"Technical note explaining the definition of the HDI"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Technical+note+explaining+the+definition+of+the+HDI&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fhdr.undp.org%2Fen%2Fmedia%2Fhdr_20072008_tech_note_1.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+Development+Index"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/> <span style="font-size:85%;">(5.54 MB)</span></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/web/products-eurostat-news/-/DDN-20170306-1?inheritRedirect=true&amp;redirect=%2Feurostat%2Fhome" rel="nofollow">New demographic datasets by 'Human Development Index (HDI)’</a></li>
<li>An independent <a class="external text" href="http://www.humansecurityindex.org/?page_id=204" rel="nofollow">HDI</a> covering 232 countries, formulated along lines of the traditional (pre-2010) approach.</li></ul>
